# TeX Theorem Inventory

## Closure_Adapted_Observers.tex

- `remarkplain` [#1] (line 105)
  - \normalfont} {
- `proposition` [Local visible calculus] `prop:local-calculus` (line 164)
  - \label{prop:local-calculus} For $\Delta\in\Sym(n)$, \begin{equation} \Phi_C(H+t\Delta)=\Phi+tV-t^2Q+O(t^3), \label{eq:local-expansion} \end{equation} where \begin{equation} V=L^{\mathsf T}\Delta L, \qquad Q=L^{\mathsf T}\Delta P\,H^{-1}\Delta L\succeq 0. \label{eq:VQ-def} \end{equation} If \begin{equation} \kappa_C(H):=-\log\det\Phi_C(H), \label{eq:kappa-def} \end{equation} then \begin{equation} D^2\kappa_C(H)[\Delta,\Delta] = \norm{\Phi^{-1/2}V\Phi^{-1/2}}_F^2+2\Tr(\Phi^{-1}Q). \label{eq:det-split} \end{equation} Moreover, \begin{equation} Q=0 \iff P^{\mathsf T}\Delta L=0. \label{eq:Q-vanish-general} \end{equation}
- `theorem` [$H$-whitened observer normal form] `thm:whitened-normal-form` (line 207)
  - \label{thm:whitened-normal-form} Let $B\in\St(n,m)$, so $B^{\mathsf T}B=I_m$, and define \begin{equation} C:=B^{\mathsf T}H^{1/2}. \label{eq:C-from-B} \end{equation} Set \begin{equation} A:=\widetilde\Delta:=H^{-1/2}\Delta H^{-1/2}, \qquad \Pi:=BB^{\mathsf T}. \label{eq:Delta-tilde} \end{equation} Then $C$ is surjective and \begin{equation} \Phi_C(H)=I_m, \qquad L_{C,H}=H^{-1/2}B, \qquad P_{C,H}=I-H^{-1/2}BB^{\mathsf T}H^{1/2}. \label{eq:normal-form-basic} \end{equation} The local visible response and quartic defect are \begin{equation} \label{eq:normal-form-VQ} \geomboxed{\begin{aligned} V&=B^{\mathsf T}AB,\\ Q&=B^{\mathsf T}A(I-\Pi)AB\succeq 0. \end{aligned}} \end{equation} Consequently, \begin{equation} D^2\kappa_C(H)[\Delta,\Delta] = \norm{B^{\mathsf T}AB}_F^2 + 2\Tr\!\bigl(B^{\mathsf T}A(I-\Pi)AB\bigr). \label{eq:det-split-whitened} \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Exact closure criterion] `cor:closure-criterion` (line 251)
  - \label{cor:closure-criterion} In the setting of Theorem~\ref{thm:whitened-normal-form}, \begin{equation} Q=0 \iff (I-\Pi)AB=0. \label{eq:closure-criterion} \end{equation} Equivalently, \begin{equation} Q=0 \iff A\Ran(B)\subseteq \Ran(B). \label{eq:invariant-subspace-criterion} \end{equation} Thus the quartic defect vanishes exactly when the visible $m$-plane is invariant under the whitened perturbation.
- `proposition` [Commutator identity] `prop:commutator-identity` (line 276)
  - \label{prop:commutator-identity} In the whitened setting of Theorem~\ref{thm:whitened-normal-form}, \begin{equation} \Tr(Q)=\norm{(I-\Pi)A\Pi}_F^2=\frac12\norm{[A,\Pi]}_F^2. \label{eq:commutator-identity} \end{equation} Hence \begin{equation} \geomboxed{D^2\kappa_C(H)[\Delta,\Delta]=\norm{B^{\mathsf T}AB}_F^2+\norm{[A,\Pi]}_F^2.} \label{eq:fisher-tight-split} \end{equation} In particular, \begin{equation} Q=0 \iff [A,\Pi]=0 \iff D^2\kappa_C(H)[\Delta,\Delta]=\norm{B^{\mathsf T}AB}_F^2. \label{eq:fisher-tight-equivalence} \end{equation}
- `remark` (line 301)
  - Equation~\eqref{eq:fisher-tight-split} gives the exact Fisher interpretation. The visible term is the Fisher curvature of the compressed perturbation. The commutator term is the hidden Fisher curvature generated by failure of the perturbation to close on the visible plane. Adapted observers are therefore precisely Fisher-tight observers.
- `definition` [Closure-adapted observer] `def:closure-adapted` (line 309)
  - \label{def:closure-adapted} Fix $H\in\Sym_{++}(n)$ and a finite family $\mathcal F=\{\Delta_a\}_{a\in A}\subset \Sym(n)$. For $B\in\St(n,m)$ set \begin{equation} D_a:=A_a:=\widetilde\Delta_a:=H^{-1/2}\Delta_aH^{-1/2}. \label{eq:family-whitened} \end{equation} We say that $B$, or equivalently the observer $C=B^{\mathsf T}H^{1/2}$, is \emph{$\mathcal F$-adapted} if \begin{equation} (I-\Pi)D_aB=0 \qquad (a\in A). \label{eq:F-adapted} \end{equation} Equivalently, $\Ran(B)$ is invariant under every $D_a$.
- `definition` [Visible and hidden curvature scores] `def:scores` (line 325)
  - \label{def:scores} For $B\in\St(n,m)$ define \begin{equation} \mathcal S(\Pi)=\mathsf S_{\mathcal F}(B):=\sum_{a\in A}\norm{B^{\mathsf T}D_aB}_F^2, \label{eq:S-def} \end{equation} \begin{equation} \mathcal L(\Pi)=\mathsf H_{\mathcal F}(B):=2\sum_{a\in A}\Tr\!\bigl(B^{\mathsf T}D_a(I-\Pi)D_aB\bigr)=\sum_{a\in A}\norm{[D_a,\Pi]}_F^2, \label{eq:H-def} \end{equation} and, whenever $\mathcal S(\Pi)+\mathcal L(\Pi)>0$, \begin{equation} \eta(\Pi)=\eta_{\mathcal F}(B):=\frac{\mathcal L(\Pi)}{\mathcal L(\Pi)+\mathcal S(\Pi)}\in[0,1]. \label{eq:eta-def} \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Single-operator exact solution] `prop:single-operator-solution` (line 343)
  - \label{prop:single-operator-solution} Let $\mathcal F=\{\Delta\}$ with whitened perturbation $D=H^{-1/2}\Delta H^{-1/2}$. Then the leakage-free rank-$m$ observers are exactly the spectral projectors of $D$ of rank $m$. Among them, the maximal visible score is attained by the span of the $m$ eigenvectors of largest $\lambda_i^2$, where $\lambda_i$ are the eigenvalues of $D$.
- `theorem` [Commuting-family reduction] `thm:commuting-family` (line 350)
  - \label{thm:commuting-family} Assume that the whitened family $\{D_a\}_{a\in A}$ is pairwise commuting. Then there is an orthonormal basis $u_1,\dots,u_n$ of common eigenvectors such that \begin{equation} D_a u_i=\lambda_{a,i}u_i \qquad (a\in A,\; 1\le i\le n). \label{eq:common-eigenbasis} \end{equation} For $I\subseteq\{1,\dots,n\}$ with $|I|=m$, set \begin{equation} B_I:=(u_i)_{i\in I}. \label{eq:BI-def} \end{equation} Then $B_I$ is $\mathcal F$-adapted, hence $\eta(B_I)=0$, and \begin{equation} \mathcal S(B_I)=\sum_{i\in I}\sum_{a\in A}\lambda_{a,i}^2. \label{eq:score-common-basis} \end{equation} Conversely, every $\mathcal F$-adapted observer of rank $m$ is the orthogonal sum of common eigenspaces of the family.
- `corollary` [Optimal exact closure in the commuting case] `cor:optimal-commuting` (line 373)
  - \label{cor:optimal-commuting} Under the hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:commuting-family}, define the common spectral energies \begin{equation} \mu_i:=\sum_{a\in A}\lambda_{a,i}^2. \label{eq:mu-def} \end{equation} If $I_\star$ indexes the $m$ largest values of $\mu_i$, then $B_{I_\star}$ maximises $\mathcal S$ among all $\mathcal F$-adapted observers of rank $m$. Equivalently, among exact-closure observers, the optimal observer is obtained by selecting the $m$ common modes of largest aggregate task energy.
- `proposition` [Insufficiency of pure $\eta$ minimisation] `prop:eta-insufficient` (line 389)
  - \label{prop:eta-insufficient} There exist noncommuting symmetric families with two rank-$m$ exact-closure observers, both satisfying $\eta=0$, but with distinct visible scores. Consequently pure $\eta$ minimisation is insufficient to select a task-optimal observer.
- `remark` (line 396)
  - The proposition is decisive at the API level. Pure $\eta$ minimisation solves the closure endpoint problem. It does not solve the general approximate-design problem. The correct public target for noncommuting families is therefore the Pareto frontier in $(\mathcal L,\mathcal S)$, or equivalently $(\eta,\mathcal S)$. A constrained selector such as maximising $\mathcal S$ subject to $\eta\le \varepsilon$ is useful, but it should sit on top of the frontier rather than replace it.
- `theorem` [Grassmannian stationarity equation] `thm:stationarity` (line 400)
  - \label{thm:stationarity} Let $\mathcal F=\{D_a\}_{a\in A}$ be a finite family of symmetric whitened perturbations and let \begin{equation} \mathcal L(\Pi):=\sum_{a\in A}\frac12\norm{[D_a,\Pi]}_F^2, \label{eq:L-pi-def} \end{equation} where $\Pi$ ranges over rank-$m$ orthogonal projectors. Then a stationary point of $\mathcal L$ on $\Gr(m,n)$ satisfies \begin{equation} \geomboxed{\Bigl[\Pi,\sum_{a\in A}[D_a,[D_a,\Pi]]\Bigr]=0.} \label{eq:stationarity-equation} \end{equation} Equivalently, the double-bracket flow \begin{equation} \dot \Pi=-\Bigl[\Pi,\sum_{a\in A}[D_a,[D_a,\Pi]]\Bigr] \label{eq:double-bracket-flow} \end{equation} preserves symmetry, idempotence, and rank, and is the intrinsic descent direction generated by commutator leakage.
- `proposition` [Total captured curvature identity] `prop:total-captured-curvature` (line 422)
  - \label{prop:total-captured-curvature} Define \begin{equation} M:=\sum_{a\in A}D_a^2. \label{eq:M-def} \end{equation} Then for every rank-$m$ projector $\Pi$, \begin{equation} \geomboxed{\Tr(\Pi M)=\mathcal S(\Pi)+\mathcal L(\Pi).} \label{eq:energy-split} \end{equation} Hence the top $m$-eigenspace of $M$ exactly maximises total captured local curvature.
- `remark` (line 439)
  - Proposition~\ref{prop:total-captured-curvature} gives the exact status of the $\sum_a D_a^2$ rule. It is exact for the wrong scalar objective whenever closure and visibility pull in different directions. The rule is therefore unsafe as a final observer in the noncommuting regime, but good as a warm start for frontier optimisation.
- `theorem` [Quotient-family refinement criterion] `thm:refinement-criterion` (line 447)
  - \label{thm:refinement-criterion} Let $\mathcal F=\{D_a\}_{a\in A}\subset\Sym(n)$, and let $U\subset\R^n$ be a common invariant subspace of dimension $m_1$. Let $\Pi_U$ be the orthogonal projector onto $U$, and compress the family to the quotient or orthogonal complement by \begin{equation} \widehat D_a:=(I-\Pi_U)D_a(I-\Pi_U)\big|_{U^{\perp}}. \label{eq:quotient-family} \end{equation} Then there exists a common invariant subspace $W$ of dimension $m_2>m_1$ with \begin{equation} U\subset W \label{eq:flag-inclusion} \end{equation} if and only if the quotient family $\{\widehat D_a\}$ has a common invariant subspace of dimension $m_2-m_1$.
- `remark` (line 464)
  - Theorem~\ref{thm:refinement-criterion} says exactly what tower language is valid. Exact closure propagates through a tower when the family admits a common invariant flag. Common invariant subspace alone is not enough.
- `proposition` [$\R^3$ flag obstruction] `prop:R3-obstruction` (line 468)
  - \label{prop:R3-obstruction} Consider \begin{equation} D_1= \begin{pmatrix} 2&0&0\\ 0&1&0\\ 0&0&-1 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad D_2= \begin{pmatrix} 3&0&0\\ 0&0&1\\ 0&1&0 \end{pmatrix}. \label{eq:R3-example} \end{equation} Then $U=\spanop(e_1)$ is common invariant, so rank-$1$ coarse closure is exact. However there is no common invariant $2$-plane containing $e_1$.
- `corollary` [Small-dimensional refinement test] `cor:small-dim-refinement` (line 492)
  - \label{cor:small-dim-refinement} In dimension $3$, with coarse rank $1$ and desired fine rank $2$, refinement exists if and only if the quotient $2\times 2$ family has a common eigenvector. For symmetric $2\times 2$ families this is equivalent to pairwise commutation of the quotient family.
- `proposition` [Quartic cancellation on an adapted bridge] `prop:bridge-consequence` (line 503)
  - \label{prop:bridge-consequence} Let \begin{equation} H_{\varepsilon}=H_0+\varepsilon^2\Delta_2+O(\varepsilon^4), \label{eq:bridge-family} \end{equation} with $H_0\in\Sym_{++}(n)$ and $\Delta_2\in\Sym(n)$. If $B\in\St(n,m)$ is $\{\Delta_2\}$-adapted at $H_0$, then for $C=B^{\mathsf T}H_0^{1/2}$, \begin{equation} \Phi_C(H_{\varepsilon})-I_m = \varepsilon^2B^{\mathsf T}A_2B+O(\varepsilon^6), \label{eq:quartic-vanishes} \end{equation} where $A_2:=H_0^{-1/2}\Delta_2H_0^{-1/2}$. In particular the quartic defect vanishes.
- `corollary` [Order upgrade for smooth spectral losses] `cor:octic-upgrade` (line 522)
  - \label{cor:octic-upgrade} Let $\Sigma_{\mathrm{exact}}(\varepsilon)$ and $\Sigma_{\mathrm{tan}}(\varepsilon)$ denote the exact and tangent visible shadows along the bridge \eqref{eq:bridge-family}. Under the hypotheses of Proposition~\ref{prop:bridge-consequence}, \begin{equation} \Sigma_{\mathrm{exact}}(\varepsilon)-\Sigma_{\mathrm{tan}}(\varepsilon)=O(\varepsilon^6). \label{eq:matrix-order-upgrade} \end{equation} If $\Psi$ is a smooth spectral functional with $\Psi(0)=0$ and $D\Psi(0)=0$, then \begin{equation} \Psi\bigl(\Sigma_{\mathrm{tan}}(\varepsilon)\bigr)-\Psi\bigl(\Sigma_{\mathrm{exact}}(\varepsilon)\bigr)=O(\varepsilon^8). \label{eq:octic-upgrade} \end{equation} Thus adaptation postpones the first smooth spectral loss by one full even order.

## Connection_Flatness.tex

- `remarkplain` [#1] (line 102)
  - \normalfont} {
- `remark` (line 247)
  - Along a smooth fixed-observer path $t\mapsto H(t)$, choose any smooth frame $Z$ of $\ker C$ and write $R:=Z^{\mathsf T}HZ$. The invariant visible-hidden cross transport is \[ B:=L^{\mathsf T}\dot H Z, \qquad J:=\Phi^{-1}B. \] Then $Q=BR^{-1}B^{\mathsf T}$. In the adapted graph gauge of Section~\ref{sec:adapted-forcing}, one has $B=K'H_{hh}$, so the coordinate $K$ packages the same fixed-observer transport sector but is not itself invariant.
- `theorem` [Fixed-observer global trivialisation] `thm:global-trivialisation` (line 304)
  - \label{thm:global-trivialisation} For fixed surjective $C$, the map \begin{equation} H\mapsto (K,\Phi,H_{hh}) \label{eq:coord-map} \end{equation} is a global diffeomorphism \begin{equation} \SPD(n)\cong \R^{m\times(n-m)}\times\SPD(m)\times\SPD(n-m). \label{eq:global-diffeo} \end{equation} Moreover, \begin{equation} \det H = \det\Phi\,\det H_{hh}, \qquad \log\det H = \log\det\Phi + \log\det H_{hh}. \label{eq:det-split} \end{equation}
- `definition` [Vertical and horizontal subspaces] `def:vert-horiz` (line 327)
  - \label{def:vert-horiz} At $H\in\SPD(n)$ define \begin{equation} \mathcal V_H:=\ker D\Phi_C(H), \qquad \mathcal H_H:=\mathcal V_H^{\perp_g}. \label{eq:vert-horiz} \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Riemannian submersion and flat connection] `thm:riemannian-submersion` (line 338)
  - \label{thm:riemannian-submersion} For fixed $C$, the visible precision map $\Phi_C:\SPD(n)\to\SPD(m)$ is a Riemannian submersion for the Fisher-Rao metrics. In adapted block coordinates the horizontal space consists exactly of pure visible-block perturbations \begin{equation} \Delta_{\mathrm{hor}}= \begin{pmatrix} \delta_{vv} & 0\\ 0 & 0 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad \delta_{vv}\in\Sym(m), \label{eq:horizontal-block} \end{equation} and the induced metric on the horizontal space is \begin{equation} g_H(\Delta_1,\Delta_2)=\tfrac12\Tr(\Phi^{-1}\delta_1\Phi^{-1}\delta_2). \label{eq:horizontal-metric} \end{equation} In particular the Fisher-orthogonal Ehresmann connection is flat.
- `remark` (line 361)
  - The flatness statement is a fixed-observer statement. It gives a canonical horizontal foliation for the fibration $\Phi_C$ and a preferred block chart, but it does not say that varying $C$ carries no topology or no geometry.
- `proposition` [Spectral and trace identities] `prop:q-spectral` (line 369)
  - \label{prop:q-spectral} Let $W:=(I-\Pi)AU$. Then \begin{equation} Q=\Phi^{1/2}W^{\mathsf T}W\Phi^{1/2}. \label{eq:Q-WTW} \end{equation} The nonzero eigenvalues of $Q$ are therefore the squared singular values of $W$, equivalently of the coupling map $(I-\Pi)A\Pi:\Ran(\Pi)\to\Ran(I-\Pi)$. Moreover, \begin{equation} \Tr(Q)=\|(I-\Pi)A\Pi\|_F^2=\tfrac12\|[A,\Pi]\|_F^2. \label{eq:trace-commutator} \end{equation}
- `remark` (line 385)
  - The spectral identity upgrades leakage from a scalar summary to a channel decomposition. The principal leakage directions are the right singular vectors of $W$ in the whitened visible coordinates. In a non-whitened gauge one should compute $Q$ directly and diagonalise it there rather than transporting eigenvectors through a congruence.
- `proposition` [Hidden-mediated commutator] `prop:hidden-commutator` (line 389)
  - \label{prop:hidden-commutator} For symmetric whitened perturbations $A_1,A_2\in\Sym(n)$, let \begin{equation} V_i:=U^{\mathsf T}A_iU, \qquad C_{\mathrm{hid}}(A_1,A_2):=U^{\mathsf T}A_1(I-\Pi)A_2U-U^{\mathsf T}A_2(I-\Pi)A_1U. \label{eq:C-hid-def} \end{equation} Then \begin{equation} U^{\mathsf T}[A_1,A_2]U=[V_1,V_2]+C_{\mathrm{hid}}(A_1,A_2). \label{eq:commutator-decomp} \end{equation} The tensor $C_{\mathrm{hid}}$ is bilinear, gauge-covariant, traceless, and skew under swapping $A_1,A_2$. It is a defect tensor measuring failure of visible algebraic closure. Its status as a curvature tensor remains open.
- `theorem` [Geodesic deviation] `thm:geodesic-deviation` (line 424)
  - \label{thm:geodesic-deviation} Let $\Phi_{\mathrm{ref}}(t)$ be the Fisher-Rao geodesic in $\SPD(m)$ with the same initial data as the projected curve $\Phi(t)$. Then \begin{equation} \Phi(t)-\Phi_{\mathrm{ref}}(t)=-\tfrac12 t^2 Q_0 + O(t^3), \label{eq:geodesic-deviation} \end{equation} where $Q_0$ is the cross-defect quadratic form at $(H_0,\Delta_0)$. If the initial velocity is horizontal, then the projection is exactly a base geodesic, as for any Riemannian submersion.
- `theorem` [Exact visible equation of motion] `thm:exact-visible-eom` (line 436)
  - \label{thm:exact-visible-eom} Along any Fisher-Rao geodesic $H(t)$, the visible precision satisfies \begin{equation} \boxed{\Phi''=\Phi'\Phi^{-1}\Phi' - Q(t).} \label{eq:exact-visible-eom} \end{equation} Equivalently, \begin{equation} \nabla_{\Phi'}\Phi'=-Q(t) \label{eq:covariant-visible-eom} \end{equation} for the Levi-Civita connection of the Fisher-Rao metric on $\SPD(m)$.
- `remark` (line 453)
  - The exact forcing term is the cross-defect quadratic form, not generic hiddenness. This is the dynamical sharpening of the static leakage picture.
- `theorem` [Vanishing criterion and fixed-$K$ slices] `thm:fixed-K` (line 462)
  - \label{thm:fixed-K} Let $H(t)$ be a smooth curve in $\SPD(n)$, written in the adapted coordinates \eqref{eq:H-factorisation}. Then \begin{equation} B(t)=0 \iff Q(t)=0 \iff K'(t)=0. \label{eq:q-zero-kzero} \end{equation} Here $B(t):=K'(t)H_{hh}(t)$ is the adapted representative of the invariant cross transport from the preceding remark. For each fixed $K\in\R^{m\times(n-m)}$, the slice \begin{equation} \mathcal M_K:=\left\{T_K\diag(\Phi,H_{hh})T_K^{\mathsf T}:\ \Phi\in\SPD(m),\ H_{hh}\in\SPD(n-m)\right\} \label{eq:MK-def} \end{equation} is totally geodesic and isometric to $\SPD(m)\times\SPD(n-m)$ with its product Fisher-Rao metric. Consequently, if $Q(0)=0$ along a Fisher-Rao geodesic, then $Q(t)=0$ for all time.
- `remark` (line 484)
  - Horizontal leaves with fixed $(K,H_{hh})$ are a natural minimal family of totally geodesic free-dynamics objects. The fixed-$K$ slices are the larger natural family currently identified.
- `theorem` [Orthogonal metric decomposition] `thm:metric-decomposition` (line 488)
  - \label{thm:metric-decomposition} In the global coordinates $(K,\Phi,H_{hh})$ the Fisher-Rao metric on $\SPD(n)$ takes the form \begin{equation} \geomboxed{ds^2=\tfrac12\Tr((\Phi^{-1}d\Phi)^2)+\tfrac12\Tr((H_{hh}^{-1}dH_{hh})^2)+\Tr(\Phi^{-1}dK\,H_{hh}\,dK^{\mathsf T}).} \label{eq:metric-decomposition} \end{equation} The visible, hidden, and coupling sectors are mutually orthogonal.
- `corollary` [Exact cross-transport formula in adapted coordinates] `cor:Q-K-formula` (line 500)
  - \label{cor:Q-K-formula} For any tangent variation in the global coordinates, \begin{equation} \geomboxed{ \begin{aligned} V&=d\Phi,\\ B&=dK\,H_{hh},\\ J&=\Phi^{-1}B,\\ Q&=BH_{hh}^{-1}B^{\mathsf T}=dK\,H_{hh}\,dK^{\mathsf T},\\ \Tr(\Phi^{-1}Q)&=\Tr(\Phi^{-1}dK\,H_{hh}\,dK^{\mathsf T}). \end{aligned} } \label{eq:Q-K-formula} \end{equation} Along a Fisher-Rao geodesic, \begin{equation} Q(t)=K'(t)H_{hh}(t)K'(t)^{\mathsf T}. \label{eq:Q-time-K} \end{equation} Consequently the exact visible equation of motion becomes \begin{equation} \boxed{\Phi''=\Phi'\Phi^{-1}\Phi' - K'H_{hh}K'^{\mathsf T}.} \label{eq:adapted-eom} \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Observer-to-observer transition law] `thm:transition-law` (line 559)
  - \label{thm:transition-law} Define \begin{equation} \widehat c:=c+K_1^{\mathsf T}a, \qquad \widehat d:=d+K_1^{\mathsf T}b. \label{eq:c-hat-d-hat} \end{equation} Then the coordinates of the second observer are given explicitly by \begin{align} A_2 &= a^{\mathsf T}\Phi_1 a + \widehat c^{\mathsf T}R_1\widehat c, \label{eq:A2}\\ B_2 &= a^{\mathsf T}\Phi_1 b + \widehat c^{\mathsf T}R_1\widehat d, \label{eq:B2}\\ D_2 &= b^{\mathsf T}\Phi_1 b + \widehat d^{\mathsf T}R_1\widehat d, \label{eq:D2} \end{align} and therefore \begin{equation} R_2=D_2, \qquad K_2=B_2D_2^{-1}, \qquad \Phi_2=A_2-B_2D_2^{-1}B_2^{\mathsf T}. \label{eq:transition-final} \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Same-observer hidden gauge] `cor:hidden-gauge` (line 590)
  - \label{cor:hidden-gauge} If $C_1=C_2=C$, then every change of adapted basis has the form \begin{equation} N= \begin{pmatrix} I & 0\\ S & T \end{pmatrix}, \qquad T\in GL(n-m). \label{eq:N-same-observer} \end{equation} Under this hidden-coordinate gauge the fixed-observer coordinates transform as \begin{equation} \Phi\mapsto \Phi, \qquad R\mapsto T^{\mathsf T}RT, \qquad K\mapsto (K+S^{\mathsf T})T^{-\mathsf T}. \label{eq:hidden-gauge-action} \end{equation} In particular, $K$ is affine hidden-gauge data, not an intrinsic observable of the fixed observer.
- `corollary` [Visible output basis change] `cor:visible-gauge` (line 617)
  - \label{cor:visible-gauge} If $C_2=gC_1$ with $g\in GL(m)$ and the adapted bases are chosen compatibly, then \begin{equation} \Phi\mapsto g^{-\mathsf T}\Phi g^{-1}, \qquad K\mapsto g^{-\mathsf T}K, \qquad R\mapsto R. \label{eq:visible-gauge-action} \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Cyclic coordinate and conserved matrix current] `thm:cyclic-current` (line 648)
  - \label{thm:cyclic-current} Set \begin{equation} B:=K'R. \label{eq:B-adapted} \end{equation} Then the Lagrangian \eqref{eq:geodesic-Lagrangian} depends on $K'$ only through $B$, and $K$ is cyclic. Its conjugate momentum \begin{equation} \geomboxed{J:=\Phi^{-1}B=\Phi^{-1}K'R} \label{eq:J-def} \end{equation} is conserved along every Fisher-Rao geodesic: \begin{equation} J'=0. \label{eq:J-conserved} \end{equation} The forcing term is therefore \begin{equation} Q=BR^{-1}B^{\mathsf T}=\Phi J R^{-1}J^{\mathsf T}\Phi. \label{eq:Q-J-formula} \end{equation} Consequently the visible dynamics takes the conserved-current form \begin{equation} \boxed{\Phi''=\Phi'\Phi^{-1}\Phi' - \Phi J R^{-1}J^{\mathsf T}\Phi, \qquad J'=0.} \label{eq:EOM-with-J} \end{equation}
- `remark` (line 680)
  - The free sector is the zero-current sector $J=0$, equivalently $B=0$, equivalently $K'=0$, equivalently $Q=0$. Horizontal motion is a sufficient special case, not the full free sector.
- `corollary` [Gauge behaviour of the current] `cor:J-gauge` (line 684)
  - \label{cor:J-gauge} Under the visible output basis change \eqref{eq:visible-gauge-action}, the conserved current transforms by left multiplication, \begin{equation} J\mapsto gJ. \label{eq:J-visible-gauge} \end{equation} Under the hidden basis change \eqref{eq:hidden-gauge-action} with $S=0$, it transforms by right multiplication, \begin{equation} J\mapsto JT. \label{eq:J-hidden-gauge} \end{equation} Under a pure hidden shear ($T=I$), $J$ is unchanged.
- `proposition` [Observer-relative reduced action] `prop:reduced-action` (line 701)
  - \label{prop:reduced-action} Eliminating $K'$ in favour of the conserved current using $K'=\Phi J R^{-1}$ gives the reduced observer-relative action \begin{equation} \mathcal L_{\mathrm{red}} = \tfrac14\Tr((\Phi^{-1}\Phi')^2) + \tfrac14\Tr((R^{-1}R')^2) + \tfrac12\Tr(\Phi J R^{-1}J^{\mathsf T}), \qquad J'=0. \label{eq:reduced-action} \end{equation} This is a reduced action on $(\Phi,R;J)$, not yet a visible-only action on $\Phi$ alone.

## Finite_Observation_MASTER.tex

- `remarkplain` [#1] (line 135)
  - \normalfont} {
- `proposition` [Reduced conductance identity] `prop:reduced_conductance_identity` (line 411)
  - \label{prop:reduced_conductance_identity} In the finite-dimensional irreducible Markov setting described above, the reduced conductance matrix of the full Donsker-Varadhan quadratic envelope coincides with that of the detailed-balance reference problem: \begin{equation} M_Q=M_G. \end{equation} Equivalently, the quadratic conductance controlling the reduced Donsker-Varadhan Hessian depends only on the dissipative sector and is blind to the skew sector.
- `remark` [Dirac-analogous factorisation of the DV Hessian] `rem:dirac-factorisation` (line 450)
  - \label{rem:dirac-factorisation} The bridge identity also admits a canonical first-order factorisation, using the principal positive square root of \(H_0\). Define \begin{equation} D := H_0^{1/2} + \tfrac{1}{2}H_0^{-1/2}\widehat{J}^T. \label{eq:dirac-operator} \end{equation} Since \(\widehat{J}\) is skew-symmetric, one has \begin{equation} D^T = H_0^{1/2} + \tfrac{1}{2}\widehat{J}H_0^{-1/2}, \end{equation} and therefore \begin{equation} D^T D = H_0 + \tfrac{1}{4}\widehat{J}H_0^{-1}\widehat{J}^T = H_{DV}. \label{eq:dirac-factorisation} \end{equation} Thus \(H_{DV}=D^T D\) exactly. Since \(H_{DV}\succ 0\) on the reduced space, \(\ker D=\{0\}\), so \(D\) is invertible. The operator \(D\) packages the detailed-balance backbone and the reduced skew channel into a single first-order object whose adjoint square recovers the full nonequilibrium fluctuation Hessian.
- `theorem` [Quadraticity of the DV correction] `thm:exact_quadraticity` (line 490)
  - \label{thm:exact_quadraticity} In the finite-dimensional irreducible Markov setting of Section~\ref{sec:setting-observable-normal-forms}, the Donsker-Varadhan Hessian decomposes as \[ \begingroup \setlength{\fboxsep}{8pt} \setlength{\fboxrule}{1.15pt} \boxed{\scalebox{1.08}{$\displaystyle H_{DV}=H_0+\Delta_{DV}$}} \endgroup \] \begin{center} where the nonequilibrium correction is \end{center} \[ \begingroup \setlength{\fboxsep}{8pt} \setlength{\fboxrule}{1.15pt} \boxed{\scalebox{1.08}{$\displaystyle \Delta_{DV}=\frac14\,\widehat J\,H_0^{-1}\widehat J^{T}$}} \endgroup \] Equivalently, \(\Delta_{DV}\) is positive semidefinite and is quadratic in the reduced skew channel with no mixed dissipative-skew term.
- `remark` [Orthogonal invariance of the quadratic correction] (line 593)
  - The identity of Theorem~\ref{thm:exact_quadraticity} is invariant under orthogonal changes of reduced Euclidean Fisher coordinates. In particular, the spectrum of \(\Delta_{DV}\), and therefore every envelope, retention, and spectral-readout quantity derived from it, is coordinate-independent within the reduced Euclidean Fisher coordinates fixed by the paper.
- `corollary` [Positivity and rank control] `cor:positivity_rank_control` (line 601)
  - \label{cor:positivity_rank_control} The nonequilibrium correction \(\Delta_{DV}\) is positive semidefinite. Moreover, \begin{equation} \operatorname{rank}(\Delta_{DV})=\operatorname{rank}(\widehat J), \end{equation} and the range of \(\Delta_{DV}\) is exactly the signal subspace generated by the reduced skew channel.
- `corollary` [Detailed-balance characterisation] `cor:db_characterisation` (line 626)
  - \label{cor:db_characterisation} The following are equivalent: \begin{enumerate} \item the generator is detailed-balance in the Fisher normal form, that is, \(J=0\), \item the reduced skew channel vanishes, that is, \(\widehat J=0\), \item the Donsker-Varadhan Hessian equals its detailed-balance reference, that is, \(\Delta_{DV}=0\). \end{enumerate}
- `theorem` [Exact block formula on \(H_0\)-invariant observed sectors] `thm:exact_converter_formula` (line 709)
  - \label{thm:exact_converter_formula} Assume that the observable sector \(U=\operatorname{Ran}\Pi\) is \(H_0\)-invariant. With notation as above, the slow observable block of the nonequilibrium correction is \begin{equation} (\Delta_{DV})_{SS} = \frac14\,J_{SS}H_{0,S}^{-1}J_{SS}^{T} + \frac14\,J_{SF}H_{0,F}^{-1}J_{SF}^{T}. \end{equation} Equivalently, relative to the chosen \(H_0\)-adapted block decomposition \(U\oplus U^\perp\), the observed correction splits into an intrinsic slow block and a hidden-return block from the complementary sector.
- `corollary` [Fast-block coercive bound] `cor:fast_block_coercive_bound` (line 744)
  - \label{cor:fast_block_coercive_bound} Assume that the fast detailed-balance block satisfies \begin{equation} H_{0,F}\succeq \mu_F I \end{equation} for some \(\mu_F>0\). Then \begin{equation} \frac14\,J_{SF}H_{0,F}^{-1}J_{SF}^{T} \preceq \frac{1}{4\mu_F}\,J_{SF}J_{SF}^{T}. \end{equation} In particular, the mixed return channel is suppressed by increasing fast-sector coercivity.
- `theorem` [Exact projector formula for orthogonal observers] `thm:exact_projector_formula` (line 804)
  - \label{thm:exact_projector_formula} For every orthogonal projector \(\Pi\) on the reduced Euclidean Fisher space, \begin{equation} V_\Pi^{DV} = \operatorname{tr}(\Pi\Delta_{DV}\Pi) = \frac14\,\|\Pi A_{DV}\|_F^2. \end{equation} Equivalently, the visible nonequilibrium content retained by \(\Pi\) is the projected Frobenius energy of the weighted signal operator \(A_{DV}\) within the orthogonal-observer class fixed in this paper.
- `remark` [Orthogonal-basis invariance of visible signal] (line 841)
  - Under an orthogonal change of reduced Euclidean Fisher basis, \(A_{DV}\mapsto O A_{DV}\) and \(\Pi\mapsto O\Pi O^T\), the value \(V_\Pi^{DV}\) is unchanged. Thus the visible signal is an invariant of the orthogonal observer class, not of a particular coordinate representative.
- `theorem` [Exact weighted Ky Fan envelope for orthogonal rank-\(d\) observers] `thm:exact_weighted_ky_fan_envelope` (line 864)
  - \label{thm:exact_weighted_ky_fan_envelope} For each \(d\in\{0,1,\dots,n-1\}\), among orthogonal rank-\(d\) projectors on the reduced Euclidean Fisher space, \begin{equation} K_d^{DV} = \frac14\sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(A_{DV})^2. \end{equation} The supremum is attained by the orthogonal projector onto the span of the top \(d\) left singular vectors of \(A_{DV}\). This is a global optimum over the orthogonal rank-constrained observer class fixed in the paper.
- `proposition` [Lipschitz stability of the envelope values] `prop:lipschitz_envelope_values` (line 895)
  - \label{prop:lipschitz_envelope_values} Let \(\Delta\) and \(\Delta'\) be positive semidefinite corrections on the same reduced Euclidean Fisher space, and let \(K_d(\Delta)\) and \(K_d(\Delta')\) denote the corresponding orthogonal rank-\(d\) envelopes. Then for every \(d\), \begin{equation} |K_d(\Delta)-K_d(\Delta')| \le \sum_{k=1}^d |\lambda_k(\Delta)-\lambda_k(\Delta')| \le d\,\|\Delta-\Delta'\|_{op}. \end{equation} In particular, the envelope values are stable under operator perturbation.
- `corollary` [Worst retained signal] `cor:worst_retained_signal` (line 916)
  - \label{cor:worst_retained_signal} Let \(m=n-1\) be the dimension of the reduced Euclidean Fisher space, and extend the singular-value list of \(A_{DV}\) to length \(m\) by zeros. Then the minimum visible nonequilibrium signal over rank-\(d\) orthogonal projectors is \begin{equation} \inf_{\operatorname{rank}\Pi=d}V_\Pi^{DV} = \frac14\sum_{k=m-d+1}^{m}s_k(A_{DV})^2. \end{equation} In particular, if \(\operatorname{rank}(A_{DV})\le m-d\), then the minimum is zero.
- `corollary` [Exact retention and hidden fractions for the optimal orthogonal rank-\(d\) envelope] `cor:exact_retention_hidden_fractions` (line 964)
  - \label{cor:exact_retention_hidden_fractions} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). Then for every observable dimension \(d\), \begin{equation} \Phi_d^{DV} = \frac{\sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(A_{DV})^2}{\sum_{k=1}^{n-1}s_k(A_{DV})^2}, \qquad 1-\Phi_d^{DV} = \frac{\sum_{k>d}s_k(A_{DV})^2}{\sum_{k=1}^{n-1}s_k(A_{DV})^2}. \end{equation} In particular, the hidden nonequilibrium content is the singular-energy tail of the weighted signal operator.
- `definition` [Weighted stable rank] `def:weighted_stable_rank` (line 989)
  - \label{def:weighted_stable_rank} The weighted stable rank of the nonequilibrium signal is \begin{equation} \operatorname{sr}(A_{DV}) := \frac{\|A_{DV}\|_F^2}{\|A_{DV}\|_{op}^2} = \frac{\sum_{k=1}^{n-1}s_k(A_{DV})^2}{s_1(A_{DV})^2}, \end{equation} for nonzero \(A_{DV}\).
- `theorem` [Stable-rank obstruction] `thm:stable_rank_obstruction` (line 1010)
  - \label{thm:stable_rank_obstruction} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). Then for every \(d\), \begin{equation} \Phi_d^{DV}\le \frac{d}{\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})}. \end{equation} Equivalently, to retain at least fraction \(\eta\) of the nonequilibrium signal, any observer must satisfy \begin{equation} d\ge \eta\,\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV}). \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Observability criterion] `cor:exact_observability_criterion` (line 1054)
  - \label{cor:exact_observability_criterion} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). Then the following are equivalent for a given observable dimension \(d\): \begin{enumerate} \item there exists a rank-\(d\) orthogonal observer in the reduced Euclidean Fisher space that sees the entire nonequilibrium signal, \item \(\Phi_d^{DV}=1\), \item \(d\ge \operatorname{rank}(A_{DV})\). \end{enumerate}
- `corollary` [Blind-observer threshold] `cor:blind_observer_threshold` (line 1069)
  - \label{cor:blind_observer_threshold} Let \begin{equation} r:=\operatorname{rank}(A_{DV})=\operatorname{rank}(\Delta_{DV}). \end{equation} Then a rank-\(d\) observer can be completely blind to the nonequilibrium correction, meaning \begin{equation} V_\Pi^{DV}=0, \end{equation} if and only if \begin{equation} d\le (n-1)-r. \end{equation} Equivalently, a \(d\)-dimensional blind observer exists if and only if the observable sector can be placed entirely inside \(\ker(\Delta_{DV})\).
- `corollary` [One-mode visibility] `cor:one_mode_visibility` (line 1098)
  - \label{cor:one_mode_visibility} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). Then the maximal rank-one visible fraction is \begin{equation} \Phi_1^{DV} = \frac{1}{\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})}. \end{equation} Thus the inverse stable rank is the best one-mode visibility of the nonequilibrium signal.
- `corollary` [Envelope monotonicity and concavity] `cor:envelope_monotonicity_concavity` (line 1122)
  - \label{cor:envelope_monotonicity_concavity} The sequence \(d\mapsto K_d^{DV}\) is non-decreasing and discretely concave: \begin{equation} K_{d+1}^{DV}-K_d^{DV} \le K_d^{DV}-K_{d-1}^{DV}. \end{equation} Equivalently, the marginal gain from increasing the observer dimension decreases monotonically with rank.
- `corollary` [Optimal hidden tail] `cor:optimal_hidden_tail` (line 1145)
  - \label{cor:optimal_hidden_tail} The minimal hidden nonequilibrium signal after the best rank-\(d\) observation is \begin{equation} K_{\mathrm{tot}}^{DV}-K_d^{DV} = \frac14\sum_{k>d}s_k(A_{DV})^2. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Equality in the stable-rank obstruction] `prop:equality_stable_rank_obstruction` (line 1162)
  - \label{prop:equality_stable_rank_obstruction} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\), and let \begin{equation} a_k:=s_k(A_{DV})^2, \qquad a_1\ge a_2\ge \cdots \ge 0. \end{equation} Then \begin{equation} \Phi_d^{DV}\le \frac{d}{\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})} \end{equation} is an equality if and only if \begin{equation} a_1=a_2=\cdots=a_d. \end{equation} The analogous statement holds for the detectability retained fraction after replacing \(A_{DV}\) by \(C_{DV}:=H_0^{-1/2}\widehat J H_0^{-1/2}\).
- `proposition` [Comparison with the unweighted envelope] `prop:comparison_unweighted_envelope` (line 1230)
  - \label{prop:comparison_unweighted_envelope} The weighted DV envelope is sandwiched between the old unweighted skew singular-energy envelope, scaled by the spectral window of the detailed-balance Hessian: \begin{equation} \frac{1}{4\mu_{\max}}\,K_d(\widehat J) \le K_d^{DV} \le \frac{1}{4\mu_{\min}}\,K_d(\widehat J). \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Alignment theorem for orthogonal observers] `thm:alignment_theorem` (line 1286)
  - \label{thm:alignment_theorem} For every orthogonal projector \(\Pi\), \begin{equation} V_\Pi^{DV} = \frac14\,\sum_{k=1}^{r} s_k(A_{DV})^2\,\|\Pi u_k\|^2. \end{equation} Equivalently, the visible nonequilibrium signal retained by \(\Pi\) is a weighted alignment score between the observer and the left singular directions of the weighted signal operator.
- `remark` [Degenerate singular subspace ambiguity in the alignment theorem] (line 1319)
  - If the singular spectrum of \(A_{DV}\) has degeneracies, the left singular directions are defined only up to orthogonal rotation inside each degenerate singular subspace. The theorem should therefore be read at the level of the corresponding invariant subspace. What is canonical is the invariant subspace itself, together with the corresponding weighted sum on that subspace, not any individual basis vector inside a degenerate block.
- `corollary` [Optimal orthogonal rank-\(d\) observer] `cor:optimal_finite_observer` (line 1333)
  - \label{cor:optimal_finite_observer} Fix an observable dimension \(d\). Let \begin{equation} U_d^\ast:=\operatorname{span}\{u_1,\dots,u_d\}, \end{equation} where \(u_1,\dots,u_d\) are the top \(d\) left singular directions of \(A_{DV}\). Let \(\Pi_d^\ast\) be the orthogonal projector onto \(U_d^\ast\). Then \begin{equation} V_{\Pi_d^\ast}^{DV}=K_d^{DV}, \end{equation} and \(\Pi_d^\ast\) is an optimal rank-\(d\) observer. If the singular value \(s_d(A_{DV})\) is strictly larger than \(s_{d+1}(A_{DV})\), then \(U_d^\ast\) is uniquely determined. More generally, let \(\sigma_\ast:=s_d(A_{DV})\). Every optimal orthogonal rank-\(d\) observer must contain the full direct sum of left-singular eigenspaces with singular value strictly larger than \(\sigma_\ast\), and the remaining dimension may be chosen arbitrarily inside the eigenspace for \(\sigma_\ast\). This is the only freedom coming from degeneracy.
- `remark` [Gap-dependent subspace stability] (line 1380)
  - The optimal value is stable under perturbation by Proposition~\ref{prop:lipschitz_envelope_values}, but the optimal subspace is stable only when the cutoff spectral gap \(s_d(A_{DV})-s_{d+1}(A_{DV})\) is positive. In the gapless case the optimal value remains stable, while the optimal \(d\)-plane need not be unique.
- `proposition` [Haar-random orthogonal-observer baseline in expectation] `thm:random_observer_baseline` (line 1396)
  - \label{thm:random_observer_baseline} Let \(\Pi\) be Haar-random among rank-\(d\) orthogonal projectors on the \(m\)-dimensional reduced Euclidean Fisher space. Then \begin{equation} \mathbb E[\Pi]=\frac{d}{m}\,I, \end{equation} and therefore \begin{equation} \mathbb E[V_\Pi^{DV}] = \frac{d}{m}\,K_{\mathrm{tot}}^{DV} = \frac{d}{m}\,\frac14\|A_{DV}\|_F^2. \end{equation} Equivalently, the expected retained fraction of a random rank-\(d\) observer is exactly \begin{equation} \mathbb E\!\left[\frac{V_\Pi^{DV}}{K_{\mathrm{tot}}^{DV}}\right] = \frac{d}{m}. \end{equation} Moreover, for each singular direction \(u_k\), \begin{equation} \mathbb E[\|\Pi u_k\|^2]=\frac{d}{m}. \end{equation}
- `definition` [Alignment gain] `def:alignment_gain` (line 1474)
  - \label{def:alignment_gain} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). For observable dimension \(d\), define the alignment gain \begin{equation} \mathcal A_d := \frac{\Phi_d^{DV}}{d/m}. \end{equation} Equivalently, \begin{equation} \mathcal A_d = \frac{m}{d}\, \frac{\sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(A_{DV})^2}{\sum_{k=1}^{m}s_k(A_{DV})^2}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Alignment-gain bounds] `prop:alignment_gain_bounds` (line 1495)
  - \label{prop:alignment_gain_bounds} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). Then for every observable dimension \(d\), \begin{equation} 1\le \mathcal A_d\le \frac{m}{\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})}. \end{equation} In particular, the optimal observer always performs at least as well as the random baseline, and the maximal possible advantage is controlled by the inverse weighted complexity of the signal.
- `corollary` [Rank-one alignment gain] `cor:rank_one_alignment_gain` (line 1545)
  - \label{cor:rank_one_alignment_gain} Assume \(A_{DV}\neq 0\). For \(d=1\), \begin{equation} \mathcal A_1=\frac{m}{\operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})}. \end{equation} Thus the one-dimensional design gain is the ambient reduced dimension divided by the weighted stable rank of the signal.
- `definition` [Shadow operator] `def:shadow_operator` (line 1608)
  - \label{def:shadow_operator} The shadow operator associated with the observer \(\Pi\) is \begin{equation} S_\Pi:=B_\Pi^{-1/2}E_\Pi B_\Pi^{-1/2}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Backbone factorisation] `prop:backbone_factorisation` (line 1618)
  - \label{prop:backbone_factorisation} For every rank-\(d\) orthogonal projector \(\Pi\), \begin{equation} H_\Pi = B_\Pi^{1/2}(I+S_\Pi)B_\Pi^{1/2}. \end{equation} In particular, the observed nonequilibrium Hessian is a positive perturbation of the observed detailed-balance Hessian by the shadow operator.
- `theorem` [Exact Gaussian comparison formulas] `thm:exact_gaussian_comparison_formulas` (line 1685)
  - \label{thm:exact_gaussian_comparison_formulas} Let \(\lambda_1,\dots,\lambda_d\) be the eigenvalues of \(S_\Pi\). Then the reverse Kullback-Leibler divergence is \begin{equation} D_{KL}\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi}\,\|\,\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) = \frac12\sum_{i=1}^{d}\Bigl(\lambda_i-\log(1+\lambda_i)\Bigr), \end{equation} and the forward Kullback-Leibler divergence is \begin{equation} D_{KL}\!\left(\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\,\|\,\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi}\right) = \frac12\sum_{i=1}^{d} \left( \log(1+\lambda_i)-\frac{\lambda_i}{1+\lambda_i} \right). \end{equation} Moreover, the squared Hellinger distance is \begin{equation} H^2\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi},\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) = 1- \frac{\det(I+S_\Pi)^{1/4}}{\det(I+\tfrac12 S_\Pi)^{1/2}}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Shadow spectrum as complete Gaussian control object] `prop:shadow_control_object` (line 1806)
  - \label{prop:shadow_control_object} For a fixed observer \(\Pi\), the observed Gaussian pair \begin{equation} \mathcal N_{DB,\Pi}, \qquad \mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi} \end{equation} is equivalent, under invertible linear whitening and orthogonal diagonalisation, to the product pair \begin{equation} \bigotimes_{i=1}^{d}\mathcal N(0,1), \qquad \bigotimes_{i=1}^{d}\mathcal N\!\left(0,\frac{1}{1+\lambda_i}\right), \end{equation} where \(\lambda_1,\dots,\lambda_d\) are the eigenvalues of \(S_\Pi\). Consequently, every invertibly invariant centred-Gaussian discrimination functional of the observed pair is determined by the shadow spectrum \(\{\lambda_i\}_{i=1}^{d}\) alone.
- `proposition` [KL and total-variation bounds] `prop:kl_tv_bounds` (line 1846)
  - \label{prop:kl_tv_bounds} For every observer \(\Pi\), \begin{equation} D_{KL}\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi}\,\|\,\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) \le \frac14\,\|S_\Pi\|_F^2. \end{equation} Consequently, \begin{equation} \operatorname{TV}\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi},\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) \le \frac{1}{2\sqrt2}\,\|S_\Pi\|_F. \end{equation} For equal priors, the optimal Bayes classification error satisfies \begin{equation} P_e^\ast \ge \frac12-\frac{1}{4\sqrt2}\,\|S_\Pi\|_F. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Backbone-normalised visibility bound] `prop:backbone_normalised_visibility_bound` (line 1914)
  - \label{prop:backbone_normalised_visibility_bound} For every observer \(\Pi\), \begin{equation} \|S_\Pi\|_{op} \le \frac{V_\Pi^{DV}}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi)}, \qquad \|S_\Pi\|_{F} \le \frac{V_\Pi^{DV}}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi)}. \end{equation} In particular, \begin{equation} \|S_\Pi\|_{op} \le \frac{K_d^{DV}}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi)}, \qquad \|S_\Pi\|_{F} \le \frac{K_d^{DV}}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi)}. \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Gaussian equilibrium-shadow criterion] `thm:equilibrium_shadow_criterion` (line 1987)
  - \label{thm:equilibrium_shadow_criterion} Let \(\Pi\) be a rank-\(d\) observer and let \(S_\Pi\) be its shadow operator. Then the observed nonequilibrium and observed detailed-balance Gaussian laws are exactly identical if and only if \(S_\Pi=0\). More generally, if \begin{equation} \Theta_\Pi:=\|S_\Pi\|_{op}\le \varepsilon, \end{equation} then \begin{equation} D_{KL}\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi}\,\|\,\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) \le \frac{d\,\varepsilon^2}{4}, \end{equation} \begin{equation} \operatorname{TV}\!\left(\mathcal N_{DB,\Pi},\mathcal N_{NESS,\Pi}\right) \le \frac{\sqrt d\,\varepsilon}{2\sqrt2}, \end{equation} and \begin{equation} P_e^\ast \ge \frac12-\frac{\sqrt d\,\varepsilon}{4\sqrt2}. \end{equation} If \begin{equation} \frac{K_d^{DV}}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi)}\le \varepsilon \end{equation} for some \(\varepsilon>0\), then the compressed Gaussian fluctuation law is quantitatively close to the corresponding detailed-balance Gaussian fluctuation law, with bounds given above in terms of \(\varepsilon\). This is a statement about observed quadratic-Gaussian statistics, not about the full microscopic dynamics.
- `theorem` [Backbone-whitened detectability equivalence] `thm:backbone_whitened_detectability_equivalence` (line 2082)
  - \label{thm:backbone_whitened_detectability_equivalence} Let \(U\subset V\) be a \(d\)-dimensional observable subspace, and let \(Q\in\mathbb R^{(n-1)\times d}\) have orthonormal columns spanning \(U\). Define \begin{equation} S_U:=(Q^T H_0 Q)^{-1/2}Q^T\Delta_{DV}Q(Q^T H_0 Q)^{-1/2} \end{equation} and \begin{equation} Y_U:=H_0^{1/2}Q(Q^T H_0 Q)^{-1/2}. \end{equation} Then \begin{equation} Y_U^T Y_U=I_d, \qquad S_U=Y_U^T T Y_U. \end{equation} Hence \begin{equation} \operatorname{tr}(S_U)=\operatorname{tr}(P_{W_U}T)=\frac14\|P_{W_U}C_{DV}\|_F^2, \end{equation} where \(W_U:=\operatorname{Ran}(Y_U)\) and \(P_{W_U}\) is the Euclidean orthogonal projector onto \(W_U\). Conversely, every Euclidean \(d\)-plane \(W\subset V\) arises as \(W=H_0^{1/2}U\) for a unique observable \(d\)-plane \(U\).
- `remark` [Detectability versus raw visibility] (line 2134)
  - Theorem~\ref{thm:backbone_whitened_detectability_equivalence} is a bijection between observable \(d\)-planes and whitened Euclidean \(d\)-planes. It is not a statement about arbitrary observation channels. Detectability here is defined relative to \(H_0\)-normalised quadratic compression and should not be conflated with raw visible signal unless additional commuting or isotropic-backbone structure is imposed.
- `corollary` [Exact detectability envelope] `cor:exact_detectability_envelope` (line 2140)
  - \label{cor:exact_detectability_envelope} Let \begin{equation} \theta_1\ge \theta_2\ge \cdots \ge \theta_{n-1}\ge 0 \end{equation} be the eigenvalues of \(T\), equivalently \begin{equation} \theta_k=\frac14 s_k(C_{DV})^2. \end{equation} Define \begin{equation} \Theta_d:=\sup_{\dim U=d}\operatorname{tr}(S_U). \end{equation} Then \begin{equation} \Theta_d=\sum_{k=1}^{d}\theta_k, \qquad \inf_{\dim U=d}\operatorname{tr}(S_U)=\sum_{k=(n-1)-d+1}^{n-1}\theta_k. \end{equation} The maximiser is the observable subspace whose whitened image is the span of the top \(d\) eigendirections of \(T\). If \begin{equation} \widetilde\Phi_d:=\frac{\Theta_d}{\operatorname{tr}(T)}= \frac{\sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(C_{DV})^2}{\sum_{k=1}^{n-1}s_k(C_{DV})^2}, \end{equation} then \begin{equation} \widetilde\Phi_d\le \frac{d}{\operatorname{sr}(C_{DV})}, \qquad \operatorname{sr}(C_{DV})= \frac{\|C_{DV}\|_F^2}{\|C_{DV}\|_{op}^2}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Canonical current-plane decomposition] `prop:canonical_current_plane_decomposition` (line 2182)
  - \label{prop:canonical_current_plane_decomposition} There exist pairwise orthogonal two-dimensional subspaces \begin{equation} E_1,\dots,E_r\subset V, \end{equation} positive numbers \begin{equation} \kappa_1\ge \kappa_2\ge \cdots \ge \kappa_r>0, \end{equation} and an orthogonal decomposition \begin{equation} V=E_1\oplus\cdots\oplus E_r\oplus \ker C_{DV}, \end{equation} such that for each \(j\), \begin{equation} C_{DV}|_{E_j}=\kappa_j R_j, \qquad R_j^T=-R_j, \qquad R_j^2=-I_{E_j}, \end{equation} and therefore \begin{equation} T|_{E_j}=\frac{\kappa_j^2}{4}I_{E_j}, \qquad T|_{\ker C_{DV}}=0. \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Paired detectability spectrum] `cor:paired_detectability_spectrum` (line 2248)
  - \label{cor:paired_detectability_spectrum} Let \begin{equation} \theta_1\ge \theta_2\ge \cdots \ge \theta_{n-1}\ge 0 \end{equation} be the eigenvalues of \(T\). Then every positive detectability eigenvalue has even multiplicity. More precisely, \begin{equation} \theta_{2j-1}=\theta_{2j}=\frac{\kappa_j^2}{4}, \qquad j=1,\dots,r, \end{equation} and all remaining eigenvalues are zero. Consequently, \begin{equation} \operatorname{rank}(\Delta_{DV}) = \operatorname{rank}(T) = \operatorname{rank}(C_{DV}) = 2r, \end{equation} so the nonequilibrium correction can never have rank one.
- `corollary` [Universal rank-one detectability ceiling] `cor:universal_rank_one_detectability_ceiling` (line 2277)
  - \label{cor:universal_rank_one_detectability_ceiling} Assume \(\operatorname{tr}(T)>0\), so that the retained fractions from Corollary~\ref{cor:exact_detectability_envelope} are defined. Then \begin{equation} \widetilde\Phi_1\le \frac12. \end{equation} Equality holds if and only if \(\operatorname{rank}(\Delta_{DV})=2\), equivalently if and only if there is exactly one nonzero current plane.
- `corollary` [Generalised eigenvalue formulation of detectability] `cor:generalised_eigenvalue_detectability` (line 2300)
  - \label{cor:generalised_eigenvalue_detectability} The nonzero eigenvalues \(\theta_k\) of \(T\) are the generalised eigenvalues of the pair \((\Delta_{DV},H_0)\): \begin{equation} \Delta_{DV}u=\theta\,H_0u. \end{equation} The optimal detectable modes may be chosen as \(H_0\)-orthonormal generalised eigenvectors \begin{equation} u_i^T H_0 u_j=\delta_{ij}, \end{equation} and \begin{equation} \Theta_d=\sum_{k=1}^{d}\theta_k. \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Detectability spectroscopy] `cor:detectability_spectroscopy` (line 2320)
  - \label{cor:detectability_spectroscopy} The cumulative detectability envelope recovers the detectability spectrum: \begin{equation} \theta_d=\Theta_d-\Theta_{d-1}. \end{equation} Hence the full backbone-normalised detectability spectrum is encoded by the hierarchy \(\{\Theta_d\}_{d=0}^{n-1}\).
- `corollary` [Rank-one detectability and the top generalised eigenmode] `thm:one_mode_detectability` (line 2336)
  - \label{thm:one_mode_detectability} The optimal one-dimensional detectable observer solves \begin{equation} \Theta_1 = \sup_{u\neq 0} \frac{u^T\Delta_{DV}u}{u^T H_0 u}. \end{equation} Equivalently, \(\Theta_1\) is the top generalised eigenvalue of the pair \((\Delta_{DV},H_0)\), or the top eigenvalue of \(T\). Thus \begin{equation} \Theta_1=\theta_1=\frac14 s_1(C_{DV})^2. \end{equation} The optimal one-mode detectable direction is any \(H_0\)-normalised generalised eigenvector satisfying \begin{equation} \Delta_{DV}u=\theta_1 H_0 u, \qquad u^T H_0 u=1. \end{equation}
- `theorem` [Two-envelope backbone spectroscopy] `thm:two_envelope_backbone_spectroscopy` (line 2362)
  - \label{thm:two_envelope_backbone_spectroscopy} Assume \begin{equation} H_0>0, \qquad \Delta_{DV}\ge 0, \end{equation} and let \begin{equation} T=H_0^{-1/2}\Delta_{DV}H_0^{-1/2}. \end{equation} Let \begin{equation} \tau_1\ge \tau_2\ge \cdots \ge \tau_{n-1}\ge 0 \end{equation} be the eigenvalues of \(\Delta_{DV}\), and let \begin{equation} \theta_1\ge \theta_2\ge \cdots \ge \theta_{n-1}\ge 0 \end{equation} be the eigenvalues of \(T\). If \begin{equation} \mu_{\min}I\preceq H_0\preceq \mu_{\max}I, \end{equation} then for every \(i\), \begin{equation} \frac{\tau_i}{\mu_{\max}} \le \theta_i \le \frac{\tau_i}{\mu_{\min}}. \end{equation} Consequently, for every \(d\), \begin{equation} \frac{K_d^{DV}}{\mu_{\max}} \le \Theta_d \le \frac{K_d^{DV}}{\mu_{\min}}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Exact commuting-case backbone spectroscopy] `prop:commuting_case_reduction` (line 2440)
  - \label{prop:commuting_case_reduction} Assume \begin{equation} [H_0,\Delta_{DV}]=0, \qquad H_0>0, \qquad \Delta_{DV}\ge 0. \end{equation} Then there exists an orthogonal basis in which \begin{equation} H_0=\operatorname{diag}(\mu_1,\dots,\mu_{n-1}), \qquad \Delta_{DV}=\operatorname{diag}(\tau_1,\dots,\tau_{n-1}), \end{equation} with \(\mu_i>0\) and \(\tau_i\ge 0\). In that basis, \begin{equation} T=H_0^{-1/2}\Delta_{DV}H_0^{-1/2} = \operatorname{diag}\!\left(\frac{\tau_1}{\mu_1},\dots,\frac{\tau_{n-1}}{\mu_{n-1}}\right). \end{equation} Hence along each common eigenvector the corresponding generalised eigenvalue is the ratio \(\tau_i/\mu_i\). Equivalently, the spectrum of \(T\) is the multiset of ratios \(\{\tau_i/\mu_i\}_{i=1}^{n-1}\), with common eigenvectors of \(H_0\) and \(\Delta_{DV}\) furnishing the modes.
- `corollary` [Isotropic-backbone reduction] `cor:isotropic_backbone_reduction` (line 2469)
  - \label{cor:isotropic_backbone_reduction} If \(H_0\) is isotropic on \(\operatorname{Ran}(\Delta_{DV})\), meaning \begin{equation} H_0=\mu I \quad\text{on } \operatorname{Ran}(\Delta_{DV}), \end{equation} then \begin{equation} T=\frac{1}{\mu}\Delta_{DV}. \end{equation} Hence raw visibility and detectability choose the same eigendirections, and their spectra differ only by the constant factor \(1/\mu\).

- `theorem` [Cumulative envelope and ordered spectral increments] `thm:cumulative_envelope_exact_spectral_increments` (line 2679)
  - \label{thm:cumulative_envelope_exact_spectral_increments} For each \(d\in\{1,\dots,n-1\}\), \begin{equation} K_d^{DV}-K_{d-1}^{DV} = \frac14\,s_d(A_{DV})^2. \end{equation} Equivalently, the ordered singular-energy profile of the weighted nonequilibrium signal is obtained by discrete differentiation of the envelope hierarchy.
- `corollary` [Recovery of the ordered singular-energy profile] `cor:exact_recovery_singular_energy_profile` (line 2713)
  - \label{cor:exact_recovery_singular_energy_profile} For each \(d\in\{1,\dots,n-1\}\), \begin{equation} s_d(A_{DV})^2 = 4\bigl(K_d^{DV}-K_{d-1}^{DV}\bigr). \end{equation} Hence the full ordered singular-energy spectrum of \(A_{DV}\) is determined exactly by the envelope hierarchy.
- `corollary` [Recovery of the nonzero spectrum of the DV correction] `cor:recovery_spectrum_DV_correction` (line 2734)
  - \label{cor:recovery_spectrum_DV_correction} The nonzero eigenvalues of \(\Delta_{DV}\) are \begin{equation} \frac14\,s_k(A_{DV})^2, \qquad 1\le k\le \operatorname{rank}(A_{DV}), \end{equation} and are recovered from the envelope increments: \begin{equation} \lambda_k(\Delta_{DV}) = K_k^{DV}-K_{k-1}^{DV}. \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Recovery of weighted stable rank] `cor:exact_recovery_weighted_stable_rank` (line 2774)
  - \label{cor:exact_recovery_weighted_stable_rank} If \(A_{DV}\neq 0\), then \begin{equation} \operatorname{sr}(A_{DV}) = \frac{K_{n-1}^{DV}}{K_1^{DV}}. \end{equation}
- `corollary` [Recovery of signal rank] `cor:exact_recovery_signal_rank` (line 2815)
  - \label{cor:exact_recovery_signal_rank} The rank of the weighted signal operator is the number of strictly positive envelope increments: \begin{equation} \operatorname{rank}(A_{DV}) = \#\{d\in\{1,\dots,n-1\}:K_d^{DV}>K_{d-1}^{DV}\}. \end{equation} Equivalently, \begin{equation} \operatorname{rank}(\Delta_{DV}) = \#\{d\in\{1,\dots,n-1\}:K_d^{DV}>K_{d-1}^{DV}\}. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Spectral completeness of the envelope] `prop:spectral_completeness_of_envelope` (line 2843)
  - \label{prop:spectral_completeness_of_envelope} The sequence \(\{K_d^{DV}\}_{d=0}^{n-1}\) determines the full singular-value list of \(A_{DV}\), and hence determines every spectral functional of \(A_{DV}\) and every spectral functional of \(\Delta_{DV}\).
- `definition` [Observability dominance] `def:observability_dominance` (line 2860)
  - \label{def:observability_dominance} We say that \(Q^{(1)}\) dominates \(Q^{(2)}\) in the strong observability order if \begin{equation} K_d^{(1)}\ge K_d^{(2)} \qquad\text{for every }d. \end{equation} We say that \(Q^{(1)}\) dominates \(Q^{(2)}\) in the normalised observability order if \begin{equation} \Phi_d^{(1)}\ge \Phi_d^{(2)} \qquad\text{for every }d. \end{equation}
- `proposition` [Spectral meaning of observability dominance] `prop:spectral_meaning_observability_dominance` (line 2878)
  - \label{prop:spectral_meaning_observability_dominance} The following are equivalent: \begin{enumerate} \item \(Q^{(1)}\) dominates \(Q^{(2)}\) in the strong observability order, \item for every \(d\), \begin{equation} \sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(A_{DV}^{(1)})^2 \ge \sum_{k=1}^{d}s_k(A_{DV}^{(2)})^2. \end{equation} \end{enumerate} In particular, strong observability dominance is weak majorisation of the squared singular-value vectors, equivalently dominance of the Ky Fan partial sums. Similarly, if the total signals agree, \begin{equation} K_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(1)}=K_{\mathrm{tot}}^{(2)}, \end{equation} then normalised observability dominance is equivalent to majorisation of the normalised singular-energy profiles.
- `corollary` [Gaussian projection suppression criterion] `thm:projection_suppression_as_corollary` (line 2949)
  - \label{thm:projection_suppression_as_corollary} Let \(\Pi\) be a rank-\(d\) observable projector. Suppose that a family of generators \(Q^{(\alpha)}\) satisfies \begin{equation} \frac{K_d^{DV}(Q^{(\alpha)})}{\lambda_{\min}(B_\Pi^{(\alpha)})}\to 0 \qquad\text{as }\alpha\to\infty. \end{equation} Then the compressed Gaussian fluctuation laws converge, in Kullback-Leibler divergence, total variation, and Hellinger distance, to the corresponding compressed detailed-balance Gaussian laws. In particular, the projected Donsker-Varadhan Hessian becomes asymptotically indistinguishable from the projected detailed-balance backbone at the observed Gaussian level.
- `corollary` [Asymptotic shared observed-Gaussian behaviour under a common projected normal form] `thm:observable_universality_from_shadow` (line 3001)
  - \label{thm:observable_universality_from_shadow} Fix an observable rank \(d\). Let \(\{Q^{(1)}_\alpha\}\) and \(\{Q^{(2)}_\alpha\}\) be two families of finite-dimensional irreducible Markov generators with the same projected normal form for each \(\alpha\): \begin{equation} N_\Pi(Q^{(1)}_\alpha)=N_\Pi(Q^{(2)}_\alpha). \end{equation} Let \(B_{\Pi,\alpha}\) denote the common projected detailed-balance backbone determined by that shared normal form, and suppose that for \(a\in\{1,2\}\), \begin{equation} \frac{K_d^{DV}(Q^{(a)}_\alpha)}{\lambda_{\min}(B_{\Pi,\alpha})}\to 0 \qquad\text{as }\alpha\to\infty. \end{equation} Then each observed Gaussian fluctuation law converges, in Kullback-Leibler divergence, total variation, and Hellinger distance, to the common projected detailed-balance Gaussian law determined by \(B_{\Pi,\alpha}\). Consequently, the two observed Gaussian laws converge to one another in total variation and Hellinger distance. In particular, the observed Gaussian equivalence class is governed asymptotically by the projected normal form once the visible nonequilibrium correction becomes negligible relative to the projected backbone.
- `theorem` [Abstract weighted envelope theorem] `thm:abstract_weighted_envelope_theorem` (line 3119)
  - \label{thm:abstract_weighted_envelope_theorem} Let \(V\) be a finite-dimensional metric space with positive-definite metric \(M\), and let \(\Delta=BB^{\sharp}\) be a positive semidefinite correction operator on \(V\). Define \begin{equation} \widetilde B:=M^{1/2}BM^{-1/2}, \qquad \widetilde\Pi:=M^{1/2}\Pi M^{-1/2}. \end{equation} Then for every \(M\)-orthogonal projector \(\Pi\), \begin{equation} V_\Pi(\Delta) = \operatorname{tr}(\Pi\Delta\Pi) = \|\widetilde\Pi\,\widetilde B\|_F^2. \end{equation} Consequently, the optimal rank-\(d\) visible signal is given by the Ky Fan top-singular-energy envelope of \(\widetilde B\), the retention fraction is the corresponding cumulative singular-energy ratio, and the effective complexity invariant is the stable rank of \(\widetilde B\).
- `proposition` [Factorisation-gauge invariance] (line 3160)
  - Suppose \(\Delta=BB^{\sharp}=\widetilde B\,\widetilde B^{\sharp}\) with \(\widetilde B=BU\) for an \(M\)-unitary operator \(U\) satisfying \(U^{\sharp}U=I\). Then the visible signal, envelope hierarchy, retention fractions, stable rank, and ordered singular-energy profile obtained after Euclideanisation are identical for \(B\) and \(\widetilde B\).
- `proposition` [Homogeneous driven ring: raw stable rank grows linearly] `prop:ring_raw_sr` (line 4534)
  - \label{prop:ring_raw_sr} For the homogeneous driven ring, \begin{equation} A_{DV}=\widehat J H_0^{-1/2} \end{equation} has squared singular values proportional to \begin{equation} \sigma_m(A_{DV})^2 \propto \frac{\sin^2 q_m}{1-\cos q_m}=1+\cos q_m=2\cos^2\!\Bigl(\frac{\pi m}{n}\Bigr), \qquad m=1,\dots,n-1. \end{equation} Consequently, \begin{equation} \operatorname{sr}(A_{DV}) =\frac{n-2}{2\cos^2(\pi/n)} \sim \frac n2. \end{equation} In particular, a one-cycle family can have raw weighted stable rank growing linearly with state-space dimension.
- `proposition` [Homogeneous driven ring: detectability complexity stays bounded] `prop:ring_detectability_sr` (line 4562)
  - \label{prop:ring_detectability_sr} For the same family, \begin{equation} C_{DV}=H_0^{-1/2}\widehat J H_0^{-1/2} \end{equation} has singular values proportional to \begin{equation} \sigma_m(C_{DV}) \propto \frac{|\sin q_m|}{1-\cos q_m}=\Bigl|\cot\!\Bigl(\frac{\pi m}{n}\Bigr)\Bigr|, \qquad m=1,\dots,n-1. \end{equation} Hence \begin{equation} \operatorname{sr}(C_{DV}) =\frac{(n-1)(n-2)}{3\,\cot^2(\pi/n)} \longrightarrow \frac{\pi^2}{3} \qquad (n\to\infty). \end{equation} Thus the same homogeneous ring that is broad in raw visibility remains bounded in backbone-whitened detectability complexity.
- `lemma` [Finite-rank skew channels force bounded complexity] `lem:finite_rank_skew_bounded_complexity` (line 4597)
  - \label{lem:finite_rank_skew_bounded_complexity} If the reduced skew channel satisfies \begin{equation} \rank(\widehat J)\le 2r, \end{equation} then \begin{equation} \rank(A_{DV})=\rank(C_{DV})\le 2r, \end{equation} and therefore \begin{equation} \operatorname{sr}(A_{DV})\le 2r, \qquad \operatorname{sr}(C_{DV})\le 2r. \end{equation}

- `definition` [Latent object and access] `def:latent-object-access` (line 269)
  - \label{def:latent-object-access} Let \(H\in\SPD(n)\) be a positive latent object and let \(C:\R^n\to\R^m\) be a surjective linear access map. Depending on the application, \(H\) may be read as a precision operator, effective stiffness, inverse covariance, information metric, or dissipative kernel. The pair \((H,C)\) specifies the latent object of the system and the part of it the observer can actually access.
- `definition` [Induced visible object] `def:induced-visible-object` (line 274)
  - \label{def:induced-visible-object} Given \((H,C)\), define the induced visible object \[ \Aobs_C(H):=(CH^{-1}C^T)^{-1}. \] This is the canonical positive object available through the access map \(C\).
- `proposition` [Variational characterisation] `prop:variational` (line 283)
  - \label{prop:variational} For every \(y\in\R^m\), \[ y^T\Aobs_C(H)y=\inf\{x^THx:\;Cx=y\}. \] Hence \(\Aobs_C(H)\) is the unique visible quadratic form recording the least latent energy needed to realise each visible displacement.
- `proposition` [Finite access descends to a quotient geometry] `prop:quotient-geometry` (line 294)
  - \label{prop:quotient-geometry} Let \(x\sim_C x'\) if and only if \(Cx=Cx'\), so that the equivalence classes are the fibres of \(\ker C\). Define \[ q_C([x]):=\inf\{z^THz:\;z\sim_C x\}. \] Then \(q_C\) is a well-defined positive quadratic form on the quotient \(\R^n/\ker C\). Under the identification of \(\R^n/\ker C\) with \(\R^m\) induced by \(C\), the matrix representing \(q_C\) is exactly \(\Aobs_C(H)\).
- `proposition` [Observation towers compose] `prop:composition` (line 305)
  - \label{prop:composition} Let \(D:\R^m\to\R^k\) be a second surjective access map. Then \[ \Aobs_D\bigl(\Aobs_C(H)\bigr)=\Aobs_{DC}(H). \] Thus observing in one stage or in two compatible stages produces the same visible object.
- `definition` [Reference object and hidden load] `def:latent-return` (line 320)
  - \label{def:latent-return} Fix a reference object \(H_{\mathrm{ref}}\) and set \[ T_C:=\Aobs_C(H_{\mathrm{ref}}). \] For any \(H\) such that \(\Ran \Aobs_C(H)=\Ran(T_C)\) and \(\Aobs_C(H)\preceq T_C\), define the hidden-load operator \[ \Lambda_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}}) := T_C^{1/2}\Aobs_C(H)^{-1}T_C^{1/2}-I. \] This is the hidden load relative to the reference object \(T_C\).
- `proposition` [Hidden-load parametrisation] `prop:hidden-load` (line 335)
  - \label{prop:hidden-load} Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:latent-return}, the operator \(\Lambda_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}})\) is positive semidefinite and \[ \Aobs_C(H)=T_C^{1/2}(I+\Lambda_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}}))^{-1}T_C^{1/2}. \] Moreover, \[ \rank \Lambda_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}})=\rank\bigl(T_C-\Aobs_C(H)\bigr), \] and the associated clock \[ \tau_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}}):=\log\det(I+\Lambda_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}})) \] satisfies \[ \tau_C(H\mid H_{\mathrm{ref}})=\log\det(T_C)-\log\det \Aobs_C(H). \]
- `proposition` [Positive perturbation] `prop:dv-bridge` (line 382)
  - \label{prop:dv-bridge} For every \(H_0\in\SPD(n)\) and every antisymmetric \(\widehat J\), the operator \[ H_{\mathrm{DV}}=H_0+\frac14\widehat J H_0^{-1}\widehat J^T \] is positive definite. Therefore every access map \(C\) induces a canonical visible object \(\Aobs_C(H_{\mathrm{DV}})\). When \(\widehat J=0\), one recovers the reference visible object \(\Aobs_C(H_0)\), and the departure from \(H_0\) is quadratic in the current sector.
- `proposition` [First visible response] `prop:first-response` (line 397)

- `proposition` [Local hidden return and visible event rate] `prop:local-birth` (line 414)
  - \label{prop:local-birth} Assume that a visible branch admits an expansion \[ X_t=tV-t^2Q+O(t^3) \] on \(S:=\Ran(V)\), with \(V|_S\succ0\) and \(Q|_S\succeq0\). Define the local ceiling \(T_t:=tV\) and the local hidden load \[ \Lambda_t:=T_{t,S}^{1/2}X_{t,S}^{-1}T_{t,S}^{1/2}-I_S. \] Then \[ \Lambda_t=tA+O(t^2), \qquad A:=V_S^{-1/2}Q_SV_S^{-1/2}\succeq0. \] Consequently, \[ \tau(\Lambda_t):=\log\det(I_S+\Lambda_t)=t\Tr(A)+O(t^2). \] We call \(\Tr(A)\) the visible event rate at onset.
- `corollary` [Quadratic onset for the current perturbation] `cor:quadratic-dv` (line 437)
  - \label{cor:quadratic-dv} If the current family has the parity expansion \[ \widehat J(\eps)=\eps \widehat J_1+O(\eps^3), \] then \[ H_{\mathrm{DV}}(\eps)=H_0+\eps^2\Delta_2+O(\eps^4), \qquad \Delta_2:=\frac14 \widehat J_1H_0^{-1}\widehat J_1^T\succeq0, \] and therefore \[ \Aobs_C(H_{\mathrm{DV}}(\eps)) = T+\eps^2V_2-\eps^4Q_4+O(\eps^6) \] for suitable \(V_2\) and \(Q_4\succeq0\) on the active support. Thus the primary interface response is quadratic in \(\eps\), while the first hidden-load term is quartic in \(\eps\).
- `proposition` [No interior reversal under monotone hidden load at fixed reference object] `prop:no-fold` (line 464)
  - \label{prop:no-fold} Fix a ceiling \(T\succeq0\) and write \(S:=\Ran(T)\). Let \[ X_\lambda=T^{1/2}(I_S+\Lambda_\lambda)^{-1}T^{1/2}, \qquad \Lambda_\lambda\succeq0, \] for a \(C^1\) path on \(S\), and define \[ \Pi_\lambda:=(I_S+\Lambda_\lambda)^{-1}, \qquad G_\lambda:=I_S-\Pi_\lambda, \qquad \tau_\lambda:=\log\det(I_S+\Lambda_\lambda). \] If \(\Lambda_\lambda'\succeq0\) for all \(\lambda\), then \[ \Pi_\lambda'=-\Pi_\lambda \Lambda_\lambda' \Pi_\lambda \preceq 0, \] \[ X_\lambda'=-T^{1/2}\Pi_\lambda \Lambda_\lambda' \Pi_\lambda T^{1/2}\preceq0, \] \[ G_\lambda'=\Pi_\lambda \Lambda_\lambda' \Pi_\lambda \succeq0, \qquad \tau_\lambda'=\Tr(\Pi_\lambda \Lambda_\lambda')\ge 0. \] Hence the canonical visible branch is monotone in Loewner order and the determinant clock cannot show an interior reversal.
- `corollary` [What an empirical interior reversal would force] `cor:empirical-fold` (line 495)
  - \label{cor:empirical-fold} Suppose a reported scalar observable is of the form \(s(\lambda)=F(X_\lambda)\) for one fixed observer, one fixed reference object, and one Loewner-monotone increasing scalar functional \(F\). If \(s\) exhibits a strict interior reversal, then at least one of the following must fail: \begin{enumerate} \item the hidden-load path is monotone, that is, \(\Lambda_\lambda'\succeq0\) for all \(\lambda\); \item the observer is fixed; \item the ceiling or reference is fixed; \item the reported scalar is actually monotone in the canonical visible object rather than produced by a non-monotone external map such as thresholding or binning. \end{enumerate}
- `remark` (line 506)
  - The strongest theorem-native statement presently available is therefore negative. The framework proves local onset and, under monotone hidden load at fixed reference, a no-interior-reversal theorem. Any robust empirical interior reversal requires an additional ingredient.
- `proposition` [A coarse observer can miss a real interface change] `prop:toy-example` (line 519)
  - \label{prop:toy-example} Let \[ H_A= \begin{pmatrix} 1&0\\ 0&4 \end{pmatrix}, \qquad H_B= \begin{pmatrix} 1&0\\ 0&1 \end{pmatrix}, \] \[ C_1=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\end{pmatrix}, \qquad C_2=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}\begin{pmatrix}1&1\end{pmatrix}. \] Then \[ \Aobs_{C_1}(H_A)=\Aobs_{C_1}(H_B)=1, \] while \[ \Aobs_{C_2}(H_A)=\frac85, \qquad \Aobs_{C_2}(H_B)=1. \] Thus the observer \(C_1\) declares no interface change at all, while \(C_2\) detects a substantial one.
- `proposition` [Collapse asymmetry under observer enrichment] `prop:collapse-asymmetry` (line 559)
  - \label{prop:collapse-asymmetry} Let \(C_1:\R^n\to\R^{m_1}\) and \(D:\R^{m_1}\to\R^{m_0}\) be surjective, and set \(C_0:=DC_1\). If \[ \Aobs_{C_1}(H_1)=\Aobs_{C_1}(H_2), \] then \[ \Aobs_{C_0}(H_1)=\Aobs_{C_0}(H_2). \] Thus equality under a richer observer descends to every coarsening.
- `proposition` [Gaussian data processing under coarsening] `prop:gaussian-dp` (line 572)
  - \label{prop:gaussian-dp} With the same notation, let \(\mu_i^{(1)}\) be the centred Gaussian distribution with covariance \(C_1H_i^{-1}C_1^T\), and let \(\mu_i^{(0)}\) be the centred Gaussian distribution with covariance \(DC_1H_i^{-1}C_1^TD^T\), for \(i=1,2\). Then \(\mu_i^{(0)}=D_\#\mu_i^{(1)}\). Consequently, for every \(f\)-divergence \(D_f\), \[ D_f(\mu_1^{(0)}\|\mu_2^{(0)})\le D_f(\mu_1^{(1)}\|\mu_2^{(1)}). \] In particular, forward Gaussian KL, reverse Gaussian KL, squared Hellinger distance, total variation distance, and Bhattacharyya distance all contract under coarsening.
- `definition` [Observer gain] `def:observer-gain` (line 581)
  - \label{def:observer-gain} Fix any contracted divergence \(\mathcal D\) on the observed centred Gaussian distributions. The gain of the richer observer \(C_1\) over its coarsening \(C_0=DC_1\) for the pair \((H_1,H_2)\) is \[ \operatorname{Gain}_{\mathcal D}(H_1,H_2;C_1\to C_0) := \mathcal D(\mu_1^{(1)},\mu_2^{(1)})-\mathcal D(\mu_1^{(0)},\mu_2^{(0)}). \] By Proposition~\ref{prop:gaussian-dp}, this quantity is nonnegative.
- `remark` (line 592)
  - The current Frobenius matrix-log score \[ D_{\mathrm{vis}}(s_1,s_2;\theta):=\norm{\log\Aobs_{C_\theta}(H_{s_1})-\log\Aobs_{C_\theta}(H_{s_2})}_F \] is useful as a practical descriptor of visible-object geometry, but no monotonicity theorem under coarsening is claimed for it here. The theorem-backed enrichment object is observer gain built from a contracted divergence on the observed Gaussian distributions.
- `proposition` [Cross-mechanism convergence] `prop:cross-mechanism` (line 734)
  - \label{prop:cross-mechanism} If consciousness is primarily an interface process, then microscopically distinct routes into unconsciousness should converge more closely at the level of the induced visible object than they do at the level of microscopic mechanism. In particular, genuinely unconscious propofol and genuinely unconscious xenon should lie closer in interface signature than either lies to wakefulness or to ketamine-like disconnected experience under matched observers.
- `remark` [What would count against it] (line 739)
  - If matched observer families fail to show interface-level convergence between genuinely unconscious propofol and xenon states, while the same methods still separate conscious from unconscious states within each agent, then the central convergence claim is weakened.
- `proposition` [Covert consciousness as observer failure] `prop:covert` (line 743)
  - \label{prop:covert} If consciousness is an active interface rather than a mere behavioural output, then some behaviourally unresponsive states should retain non-trivial interface structure under a better observer. Coarse observers should therefore under-diagnose consciousness in at least a subset of cases.
- `remark` [What would count against it] (line 748)
  - If task-matched, multimodal, or otherwise enriched observers do not recover any systematic residual structure in imagery-positive or clinically covert cases beyond what coarse resting observers already show, then the observer-failure thesis is weakened.
- `proposition` [Recovery is path-dependent] `prop:hysteresis` (line 752)
  - \label{prop:hysteresis} Loss and recovery of consciousness should not be exact reverses of one another. The route back into consciousness should show hysteresis in visible-object coordinates, hidden-load coordinates, or both, even when coarse behavioural labels match.
- `remark` [What would count against it] (line 757)
  - If longitudinal trajectories through induction and emergence collapse onto the same path in interface-level coordinates whenever behavioural labels are matched, then the hysteresis claim is weakened.
- `corollary` [Single-modality assessment is structurally fragile] `cor:single-modality` (line 761)
  - \label{cor:single-modality} Resting-only observers should be more prone to coarsening illusion than observers that combine rest with an evoked or task-matched component. Multimodal observers should therefore recover consciousness structure more faithfully than single coarse observers.
- `remark` [What would count against it] (line 766)
  - If adding evoked or task-matched access fails to improve interface-level separation or to reduce false collapse relative to resting-only observers in the relevant cohorts, then the multimodal claim is weakened.

## Geometric_Observation_MASTER.tex

- `remarkplain` [#1] (line 99)
